CNN Election 2000 Coverage

PRESIDENT DOLE RE-ELECTED BY CLOSE MARGIN; MULTIPLE STATES YET TO BE CALLED. GEPHARDT CONCEDES.

\n\nPresident Robert J. Dole of Kansas, at the age of 77 years old, has been re-elected, winning his party a second term in the Oval Office, in a close election against the Speaker of the House, Richard Gephardt. In a stark comparison to four years ago, Dole is expected to win the popular vote against his challenger; however, due to the election being close, this can shift; however, his lead is unlikely to change.

\nAccording to sources within the Gephardt campaign, they calculated around an hour ago that it was mathematically impossible for them to defeat the President. That is when he began to prepare his concession speech, which he is set to deliver in under a half hour from now. He also gave a concession phone call to President Dole about 5 minutes ago. Dole reportedly received the call with grace and even cracked a few jokes with him.

It seems the House of Representatives will stay in control of the Democratic Party for at least two more years. The Senate meanwhile, has been projected to remain in GOP control, therefore retaining the divided government which was established in the 1998 midterms.

This election marks the beginning of the end of an era as Dole, a decorated World War II veteran, is almost certainly going to be the final president from the Greatest Generation. He is expected to give his victory speech shortly after Gephardt gives his concession speech. He will be sworn in for his second term on January 20th, 2001, and will serve until January 20th, 2005, as he is term limited. CNN will cover his second inauguration and any potential cabinet changes in the coming days, so please stay tuned.

CNN Election 2000 Coverage

\n

DOLE RE-ELECTED DECISIVELY; THE PRESIDENT SWEEPS THROUGHOUT MOST SWING STATES. A HUMILIATED GEPHARDT CONCEDES.

\n\nPresident Robert J. Dole of Kansas, at the age of 77 years old, has been re-elected, winning his party a second term in the Oval Office, in a close election against the Speaker of the House, Richard Gephardt. In a stark comparison to four years ago, Dole is expected to win the popular vote against his challenger; this is not expected to shift at all, as Dole has won decisively in the electoral college vote.

According to sources within the Gephardt campaign, they calculated around two hours ago that it was mathematically impossible for them to defeat the President. That is when he began to prepare his concession speech, which he is set to deliver in under a half hour from now. They also knew things were going wrong fairly early in the night after obtaining exit poll results in multiple swing states. He gave a concession phone call to President Dole about 5 minutes ago. Dole reportedly received the call with grace and even cracked a few jokes with him. However, Gephardt understandably entered the call with a terrible mood.

It seems the House of Representatives will stay in control of the Democratic Party for at least two more years; however, their majority has been whittled down considerably. The Senate meanwhile, has been projected to remain in GOP control, therefore retaining the divided government which was established in the 1998 midterms.

This election marks the beginning of the end of an era as Dole, a decorated World War II veteran, is almost certainly going to be the final president from the Greatest Generation. He is expected to give his victory speech shortly after Gephardt gives his concession speech. The President-elect is expected to give his victory speech shortly after Dole gives his concession speech. He will be sworn in for his first term on January 20th, 2001, and will serve that term until January 20th, 2005, upon which he is eligible for a second term. CNN will cover his inauguration and his cabinet nominations in the coming days, so please stay tuned.
